</div>\n  <div class="noprint" id="mw-head-base">\n  </div>\n  <div class="mw-body" id="content" role="main">\n   <a id="top">\n   </a>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="siteNotice">\n    <!-- CentralNotice -->\n   </div>\n   <div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n   </div>\n   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">\n    CubeSat\n   </h1>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">\n     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n    </div>\n    <div id="contentSub">\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">\n     Jump to:\n     <a href="#mw-head">\n      navigation\n     </a>\n     ,\n     <a href="#p-search">\n      search\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">\n     <div class="mw-parser-output">\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ncube2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="446" data-file-width="500" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ncube2.jpg/220px-Ncube2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ncube2.jpg/330px-Ncube2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ncube2.jpg/440px-Ncube2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ncube2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/NCube_(satellite)" title="NCube (satellite)">\n          Ncube-2\n         </a>\n         , a Norwegian CubeSat (10\xc2\xa0cm cube)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <b>\n        CubeSat\n       </b>\n       (\n       <i>\n        U-class spacecraft\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpaceNews-2015-06-08_1-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SpaceNews-2015-06-08-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ) is a type of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miniaturized_satellite" title="Miniaturized satellite">\n        miniaturized satellite\n       </a>\n       for\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_research" title="Space research">\n        space research\n       </a>\n       that is made up of multiples of 10\xc3\x9710\xc3\x9710\xc2\xa0cm cubic units. CubeSats have a mass of no more than 1.33 kilograms per unit,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specs_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-specs-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and often use\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_off-the-shelf" title="Commercial off-the-shelf">\n        commercial off-the-shelf\n       </a>\n       (COTS) components for their\n       <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">\n        electronics\n       </a>\n       and structure. CubeSats are most commonly put in orbit by deployers on the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       , or launched as\n       <a href="/wiki/Secondary_payload" title="Secondary payload">\n        secondary payload\n       </a>\n       s on a\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_vehicle" title="Launch vehicle">\n        launch vehicle\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-database_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-database-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1999,\n       <a href="/wiki/California_Polytechnic_State_University" title="California Polytechnic State University">\n        California Polytechnic State University\n       </a>\n       (Cal Poly) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">\n        Stanford University\n       </a>\n       developed the CubeSat specifications to promote and develop the skills necessary for the design, manufacture, and testing of small satellites intended for\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        low Earth orbit\n       </a>\n       (LEO) that perform a number of scientific research functions and explore new space technologies. Academia accounted for the majority of CubeSat launches until 2013, when over half of launches were for non-academic purposes, and by 2014 most newly deployed CubeSats were for commercial or amateur projects.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-database_3-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-database-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       CubeSats have been built by large and small companies alike, while other projects have been the subject of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kickstarter" title="Kickstarter">\n        Kickstarter\n       </a>\n       campaigns.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Uses typically involve experiments which can be miniaturized or serve purposes such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth_observation" title="Earth observation">\n        Earth observation\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio_satellite" title="Amateur radio satellite">\n        amateur radio\n       </a>\n       . Many CubeSats are used to demonstrate spacecraft technologies that are targeted for use in small satellites or that present questionable feasibility and are unlikely to justify the cost of a larger satellite. Scientific experiments with questionable underlying theory may also find themselves aboard CubeSats as their low cost could justify riskier experiments. Biological research payloads have been flown on several missions, with more planned.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abio_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-abio-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Several missions to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">\n        Moon\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       are planned to use CubeSats.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some CubeSats became\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_first_satellites_by_country" title="Timeline of first satellites by country">\n        the first national satellites of their countries\n       </a>\n       , being launched by universities, state, or private companies.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#History">\n          <span       </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#Antennas">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.7\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Antennas\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">\n           <a href="#Thermal_management">\n    <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#Costs">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.9\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n      <span class="toctext">\n             QB50\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19">\n           <a CubeSats\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20">\n           <a href="#CubeSat_Launch_Initiative">\n            <span           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23">\n         <a href="#Launch_and_deployment">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Launch and deployment\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24">\n           <a href="#Current_launch_systems">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Current launch systems\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25">\n           <a href="#Future_and_proposed_launch_systems">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n  </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CubeSat_in_hand.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/CubeSat_in_hand.jpg/220px-CubeSat_in_hand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/CubeSat_in_hand.jpg/330px-CubeSat_in_hand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/CubeSat_in_hand.jpg/440px-CubeSat_in_hand.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CubeSat_in_hand.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         1U CubeSat structure\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The CubeSat\n       <a href="/wiki/Reference_design" title="Reference design">\n        reference design\n       </a>\n       was proposed in 1999 by professors\n       <a href="/wiki/Jordi_Puig-Suari" title="Jordi Puig-Suari">\n        Jordi Puig-Suari\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/California_Polytechnic_State_University" title="California Polytechnic State University">\n        California Polytechnic State University\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bob_Twiggs" title="Bob Twiggs">\n        Bob Twiggs\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">\n        Stanford University\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tiny_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Tiny-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Helvajian2008_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Helvajian2008-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :159\n       </sup>\n       The goal was to enable\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graduate_student" title="Graduate student">\n        graduate students\n       </a>\n       to be able to design, build, test and operate in space a\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">\n        spacecraft\n       </a>\n       with capabilities similar to that of the first spacecraft,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sputnik" title="Sputnik">\n        Sputnik\n       </a>\n       . The CubeSat, as initially proposed, did not set out to become a standard; rather, it became a standard over time by a process of\n       <a href="/wiki/Emergence" title="Emergence">\n        emergence\n       </a>\n       . The first CubeSats were launched in June 2003 on a\n       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">\n        Russian\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurockot" title="Eurockot">\n        Eurockot\n       </a>\n       , and approximately 75 CubeSats had been placed into orbit by 2012.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20120813_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sn20120813-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The need for such a small-factor satellite became apparent in 1998 as a result of work done at Stanford University\'s Space System Development Laboratory. At SSDL, students had been working on the\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=OPAL_(Spacecraft)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="OPAL (Spacecraft) (page does not exist)">\n        OPAL\n       </a>\n       (Orbiting Picosatellite Automatic Launcher) microsatellite since 1995. OPAL\'s mission to deploy daughter-ship "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Picosatellite" title="Picosatellite">\n        picosatellites\n       </a>\n       " had resulted in the development of a launcher system that was "hopelessly complicated" and could only be made to work "most of the time". With the project\'s delays mounting, Twiggs sought out\n       <a href="/wiki/DARPA" title="DARPA">\n        DARPA\n       </a>\n       funding that resulted in the redesign of the launching mechanism into a simple pusher plate concept with the satellites held in place by a spring-loaded door.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Helvajian2008_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Helvajian2008-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :151\xe2\x80\x93157\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Desiring to shorten the development cycle experienced on OPAL and inspired by the picosatellites OPAL carried, Twiggs set out to find "how much could you reduce the size and still have a practical satellite". The picosatellites on OPAL were 10.1\xc3\x977.6\xc3\x972.5\xc2\xa0cm, a size that was not conducive to covering all sides of the spacecraft with solar cells. Inspired by a 4-inch cubic plastic box used to display\n       <a href="/wiki/Beanie_Babies" title="Beanie Babies">\n        Beanie Babies\n       </a>\n       in stores,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abio_5-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-abio-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Twiggs first settled on the larger 10-centimeter cube as a guideline for the new (yet-to-be-named) CubeSat concept. A model of a launcher was developed for the new satellite using the same pusher plate concept that had been used in the modified OPAL launcher. Twiggs presented the idea to Puig-Suari in the summer of 1999 and then at the Japan-U.S. Science, Technology and Space Applications Program (JUSTSAP) conference in November 1999.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Helvajian2008_8-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Helvajian2008-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :157\xe2\x80\x93159\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The term "CubeSat" was coined to denote\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miniaturized_satellite#Nanosatellite" title="Miniaturized satellite">\n        nanosatellites\n       </a>\n       that adhere to the standards described in the CubeSat design specification. Cal Poly published the standard in an effort led by aerospace engineering professor Jordi Puig-Suari.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiny_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tiny-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Bob_Twiggs" title="Bob Twiggs">\n        Bob Twiggs\n       </a>\n       , of the Department of Aeronautics &amp; Astronautics at Stanford University, and currently a member of the space science faculty at Morehead State University in Kentucky, has contributed to the CubeSat community.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       His efforts have focused on CubeSats from educational institutions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cnn-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The specification does not apply to other cube-like nanosatellites such as the NASA "MEPSI" nanosatellite, which is slightly larger than a CubeSat. GeneSat-1 was NASA\'s first fully automated, self-contained biological spaceflight experiment on a satellite of its size. It was also the first U.S. launched CubeSat. This work, lead by John Hines, at NASA Ames Research was the catalyst for the entire NASA CubeSat program.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Design">\n        Design\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Design">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The CubeSat specification accomplishes several high-level goals. The main reason for miniaturizing satellites is to reduce the cost of deployment and are often suitable for launch in multiples, using the excess capacity of larger launch vehicles. The CubeSat design specifically minimizes risk to the rest of the launch vehicle and payloads. Encapsulation of the launcher\xe2\x80\x93\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Payload_(air_and_space_craft)" title="Payload (air and space craft)">\n        payload\n       </a>\n       interface takes away the amount of work that would previously be required for mating a piggyback satellite with its launcher. Unification among payloads and launchers enables quick exchanges of payloads and utilization of launch opportunities on short notice.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Standard CubeSats are made up of 10\xc3\x9710\xc3\x9711.35\xc2\xa0cm units designed to provide 10\xc3\x9710\xc3\x9710\xc2\xa0cm or 1 liter of useful volume while weighing no more than 1.33\xc2\xa0kg (2.9\xc2\xa0lb) per unit. The smallest standard size is 1U, while 3U+ is the largest being composed of three units stacked lengthwise with an additional 6.4\xc2\xa0cm diameter cylinder centered on the long axis and extending 3.6\xc2\xa0cm beyond one face.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specs_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-specs-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Aerospace_Corporation" title="The Aerospace Corporation">\n        The Aerospace Corporation\n       </a>\n       has constructed and launched two smaller form CubeSats of 0.5U for radiation measurement and technological demonstration.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In recent years larger CubeSat platforms have been proposed, most commonly 6U (10\xc3\x9720\xc3\x9730\xc2\xa0cm or 12\xc3\x9724\xc3\x9736\xc2\xa0cm\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-threeumaxdefinition_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-threeumaxdefinition-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ) and 12U (20x20x30\xc2\xa0cm or 24x24x36\xc2\xa0cm\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-threeumaxdefinition_15-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-threeumaxdefinition-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ), to extend the capabilities of CubeSats beyond academic and technology validation applications and into more complex science and national defense goals. In 2014 two 6U\n       <a href="/wiki/Perseus-M" title="Perseus-M">\n        Perseus-M\n       </a>\n       CubeSats were launched for maritime surveillance, those two CubeSats represent the largest CubeSats flown as of 2015. The 2018 launch of the\n       <a href="/wiki/InSight" title="InSight">\n        InSight\n       </a>\n       lander to Mars, will include two 6U CubeSats called\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Cube_One" title="Mars Cube One">\n        Mars Cube One\n       </a>\n       (MarCO).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scientist_holding_a_CubeSat.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3307" data-file-width="2472" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Scientist_holding_a_CubeSat.jpg/220px-Scientist_holding_a_CubeSat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Scientist_holding_a_CubeSat.jpg/330px-Scientist_holding_a_CubeSat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Scientist_holding_a_CubeSat.jpg/440px-Scientist_holding_a_CubeSat.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scientist_holding_a_CubeSat.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Scientist holding a CubeSat chassis\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Since nearly all CubeSats are 10\xc3\x9710\xc2\xa0cm (regardless of length) they can all be launched and deployed using a common deployment system called a Poly-PicoSatellite Orbital Deployer (P-POD), developed and built by Cal Poly.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       No electronics\n       <a href="/wiki/Computer_form_factor" title="Computer form factor">\n        form factors\n       </a>\n       or communications protocols are specified or required by the CubeSat Design Specification, but COTS hardware has consistently utilized certain features which many treat as standards in CubeSat electronics. Most COTS and custom designed electronics fit the form of\n       <a href="/wiki/PC/104" title="PC/104">\n        PC/104\n       </a>\n       , which was not designed for CubeSats but presents a 90 \xc3\x97 96\xc2\xa0mm profile that allows most of the spacecraft\'s volume to be occupied. Technically, the PCI-104 form is the variant of PC/104 used\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the actual\n       <a href="/wiki/Pinout" title="Pinout">\n        pinout\n       </a>\n       used does not reflect the pinout specified in the PCI-104 standard. Stackthrough connectors on the boards allow for simple assembly and electrical interfacing and most manufacturers of CubeSat electronics hardware hold to the same signal arrangement, but some products do not, so care must be taken to ensure consistent signal and power arrangements to prevent damage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Care must be taken in electronics selection to ensure the devices can tolerate the radiation present. For very\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        low Earth orbits\n       </a>\n       (LEO) in which atmospheric reentry would occur in just days or weeks,\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">\n        radiation\n       </a>\n       can largely be ignored and standard consumer grade electronics may be used. Consumer electronic devices can survive LEO radiation for that time as the chance of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Single_event_upset" title="Single event upset">\n        single event upset\n       </a>\n       (SEU) is very low. Spacecraft in a sustained low Earth orbit lasting months or years are at risk and only fly hardware designed for and tested in irradiated environments. Missions beyond low Earth orbit or which would remain in low Earth orbit for many years must use\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation_hardening" title="Radiation hardening">\n        radiation-hardened\n       </a>\n       devices.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Further considerations are made for operation in high vacuum due to the effects of\n       <a href="/wiki/Sublimation_(phase_transition)" title="Sublimation (phase transition)">\n        sublimation\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Outgassing" title="Outgassing">\n        outgassing\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Whisker_(metallurgy)" title="Whisker (metallurgy)">\n        metal whiskers\n       </a>\n       , which may result in mission failure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Different classifications are used to categorize such\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miniaturized_satellite" title="Miniaturized satellite">\n        miniature satellites\n       </a>\n       based on mass.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greek_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Greek-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       1U CubeSats belong to the genre of picosatellites.\n      </p>\n      <ol>\n       <li>\n        Minisatellite (100\xe2\x80\x93500\xc2\xa0kg)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Microsatellite (10\xe2\x80\x93100\xc2\xa0kg)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Nanosatellite (1\xe2\x80\x9310\xc2\xa0kg)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Picosatellite (0.1\xe2\x80\x931\xc2\xa0kg)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Femtosatellite (0.01\xe2\x80\x930.1\xc2\xa0kg)\n       </li>\n      </ol>\n      <p>\n       Most CubeSats carry one or two\n       <a href="/wiki/Measuring_instrument" title="Measuring instrument">\n        scientific instruments\n       </a>\n       as their primary mission\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Payload_(air_and_space_craft)" title="Payload (air and space craft)">\n        payload\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">\n        Structure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Structure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cubesatkit_1u-skeleton.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="305" data-file-width="300" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Cubesatkit_1u-skeleton.jpg/220px-Cubesatkit_1u-skeleton.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/11/Cubesatkit_1u-skeleton.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cubesatkit_1u-skeleton.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A skeletonized 1U structure with computer offered by Pumpkin Inc.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n          <a href="#cite_note-24">\n           [24]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The number of joined units classifies the size of CubeSats and according to the CubeSat Design Specification and are\n       <a href="/wiki/Scalability" title="Scalability">\n        scalable\n       </a>\n       along only one axis to fit the forms of 0.5U, 1U, 1.5U, 2U, or 3U. All the standard sizes of CubeSat have been built and launched, and represent the form factors for nearly all launched CubeSats as of 2015.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Materials used in the structure must feature the same\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coefficient_of_thermal_expansion" title="Coefficient of thermal expansion">\n        coefficient of thermal expansion\n       </a>\n       as the deployer to prevent jamming. Specifically, allowed materials are four aluminum alloys:\n       <a href="/wiki/7075_aluminium_alloy" title="7075 aluminium alloy">\n        7075\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/6061_aluminium_alloy" title="6061 aluminium alloy">\n        6061\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/5005_aluminium_alloy" title="5005 aluminium alloy">\n        5005\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/5052_aluminium_alloy" title="5052 aluminium alloy">\n        5052\n       </a>\n       . Aluminum used on the structure which contacts the P-POD must be anodized to prevent\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold_welding" title="Cold welding">\n        cold welding\n       </a>\n       , and other materials may be used for the structure if a waiver is obtained.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specs_2-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-specs-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Beyond cold welding, further consideration is put into material selection as not all materials can be\n       <a href="/wiki/Materials_for_use_in_vacuum" title="Materials for use in vacuum">\n        used in vacuums\n       </a>\n       . Structures often feature soft dampers at each end, typically made of rubber, to lessen the effects of impacting other CubeSats in the P-POD.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Protrusions beyond the maximum dimensions are allowed by the standard specification, to a maximum of 6.5\xc2\xa0mm beyond each side. Any protrusions may not interfere with the deployment rails and are typically occupied by antennas and solar panels. In Revision 13 of the CubeSat Design Specification an extra available volume was defined for use on 3U projects. The additional volume is made possible by space typically wasted in the P-POD Mk III\'s spring mechanism. 3U CubeSats which utilize the space are designated 3U+ and may place components in a cylindrical volume centered on one end of the CubeSat. The cylindrical space has a maximum diameter of 6.4\xc2\xa0cm and a height no greater than 3.6\xc2\xa0cm while not allowing for any increase in mass beyond the 3U\'s maximum of 4\xc2\xa0kg. Propulsion systems and antennas are the most common components that might require the additional volume, though the payload sometimes extends into this volume. Deviations from the dimension and mass requirements can be waived following application and negotiation with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_service_provider" title="Launch service provider">\n        launch service provider\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specs_2-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-specs-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       CubeSat structures do not have all the same strength concerns as larger satellites do, as they have the added benefit of the deployer supporting them structurally during launch. Still, some CubeSats will undergo\n       <a href="/wiki/Structural_dynamics" title="Structural dynamics">\n        vibration analysis\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Structural_analysis" title="Structural analysis">\n        structural analysis\n       </a>\n       to ensure that components unsupported by the P-POD remain structurally sound throughout the launch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Despite rarely undergoing the analysis that larger satellites do, CubeSats rarely fail due to mechanical issues.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Computing">\n        Computing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Computing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Like larger satellites, CubeSats often feature multiple computers handling different tasks in\n       <a href="/wiki/Parallel_computing" title="Parallel computing">\n        parallel\n       </a>\n       including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Attitude_control" title="Attitude control">\n        attitude control\n       </a>\n       , power management, payload operation, and primary control tasks. COTS attitude control systems typically include their own computer, as do the power management systems. Payloads must be able to interface with the primary computer to be useful, which sometimes requires the use of another small computer. This may be due to limitations in the primary computer\'s ability to control the payload with limited communication protocols, to prevent overloading the primary computer with raw data handling, or to ensure payload\'s operation continues uninterrupted by the spacecraft\'s other computing needs such as communication. Still, the primary computer may be used for payload related tasks, which might include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Image_processing" title="Image processing">\n        image processing\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Data_analysis" title="Data analysis">\n        data analysis\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Data_compression" title="Data compression">\n        data compression\n       </a>\n       . Tasks which the primary computer typically handles include the delegation of tasks to the other computers, attitude control, calculations for\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_maneuver" title="Orbital maneuver">\n        orbital maneuvers\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Scheduling_(computing)" title="Scheduling (computing)">\n        scheduling\n       </a>\n       , and activation of active thermal control components. CubeSat computers are highly susceptible to radiation and builders will take special steps to ensure proper operation in the high radiation of space, such as the use of the\n       <a href="/wiki/ECC_memory" title="ECC memory">\n        ECC RAM\n       </a>\n       . Some satellites may incorporate\n       <a href="/wiki/Redundancy_(engineering)" title="Redundancy (engineering)">\n        redundancy\n       </a>\n       by implementing multiple primary computers, this could be done on valuable missions to lessen the risk of mission failure. Consumer\n       <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">\n        smartphones\n       </a>\n       have been used for computing in some CubeSats, such as NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/PhoneSat" title="PhoneSat">\n        PhoneSats\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Attitude_control">\n        Attitude control\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Attitude control">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:256px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Near_Earth_Asteroid_Scout.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="814" data-file-width="1200" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Near_Earth_Asteroid_Scout.jpg/254px-Near_Earth_Asteroid_Scout.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Near_Earth_Asteroid_Scout.jpg/381px-Near_Earth_Asteroid_Scout.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Near_Earth_Asteroid_Scout.jpg/508px-Near_Earth_Asteroid_Scout.jpg 2x" width="254"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Near_Earth_Asteroid_Scout.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Near-Earth_Asteroid_Scout" title="Near-Earth Asteroid Scout">\n          Near-Earth Asteroid Scout\n         </a>\n         concept: a controllable\n         <a href="/wiki/Solar_sail" title="Solar sail">\n          solar sail\n         </a>\n         CubeSat\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Attitude_control" title="Attitude control">\n        Attitude control\n       </a>\n       for CubeSats relies on miniaturizing technology without significant performance degradation. Tumbling typically occurs as soon as a CubeSat is deployed, due to asymmetric deployment forces and bumping with other CubeSats. Some CubeSats operate normally while tumbling, but those that require pointing in a certain direction or cannot operate safely while spinning, must be detumbled. Systems that perform attitude determination and control include\n       <a href="/wiki/Reaction_wheel" title="Reaction wheel">\n        reaction wheels\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Magnetorquer" title="Magnetorquer">\n        magnetorquers\n       </a>\n       , thrusters,\n       <a href="/wiki/Star_tracker" title="Star tracker">\n        star trackers\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sun_sensor" title="Sun sensor">\n        Sun sensors\n       </a>\n       , Earth sensors,\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_rate_sensor" title="Angular rate sensor">\n        angular rate sensors\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/GPS_navigation_device" title="GPS navigation device">\n        GPS receivers and antennas\n       </a>\n       . Combinations of these systems are typically seen in order to take each method\'s advantages and mitigate their shortcomings.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reaction_wheels" title="Reaction wheels">\n        Reaction wheels\n       </a>\n       are commonly utilized for their ability to impart relatively large\n       <a href="/wiki/Moment_(physics)" title="Moment (physics)">\n        moments\n       </a>\n       for any given energy input, but reaction wheel\'s utility is limited due to saturation, the point at which a wheel cannot spin faster. Examples of CubeSat reaction wheels include the Maryland Aerospace MAI-101\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the Sinclair Interplanetary RW-0.03-4.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Reaction wheels can be desaturated with the use of thrusters or magnetorquers. Thrusters can provide large moments by imparting a\n       <a href="/wiki/Couple_(mechanics)" title="Couple (mechanics)">\n        couple\n       </a>\n       on the spacecraft but inefficiencies in small propulsion systems cause thrusters to run out of fuel rapidly. Commonly found on nearly all CubeSats are magnetorquers which run electricity through a\n       <a href="/wiki/Solenoid" title="Solenoid">\n        solenoid\n       </a>\n       to take advantage of Earth\'s magnetic field to produce a\n       <a href="/wiki/Moment_(physics)" title="Moment (physics)">\n        turning moment\n       </a>\n       . Attitude-control modules and solar panels typically feature built-in magnetorquers. For CubeSats that only need to detumble, no attitude determination method beyond an\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_rate_sensor" title="Angular rate sensor">\n        angular rate sensor\n       </a>\n       or electronic\n       <a href="/wiki/Gyroscope" title="Gyroscope">\n        gyroscope\n       </a>\n       is necessary.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Pointing in a specific direction is necessary for Earth observation, orbital maneuvers, maximizing solar power, and some scientific instruments. Directional pointing accuracy can be achieved by sensing Earth and its horizon, the Sun, or specific stars. Sinclair Interplanetary\'s SS-411 sun sensor\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and ST-16 star tracker\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       both have applications for CubeSats and have flight heritage. Pumpkin\'s Colony I Bus uses an aerodynamic wing for passive attitude stabilization.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Determination of a CubeSat\'s location can be done through the use of on-board GPS, which is relatively expensive for a CubeSat, or by relaying radar tracking data to the craft from Earth-based tracking systems.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Propulsion">\n        Propulsion\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Propulsion">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       CubeSat propulsion has made rapid advancements in the following technologies:\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold_gas_thruster" title="Cold gas thruster">\n        cold gas\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_engine" title="Rocket engine">\n        chemical propulsion\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Electrically_powered_spacecraft_propulsion" title="Electrically powered spacecraft propulsion">\n        electric propulsion\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_sail" title="Solar sail">\n        solar sails\n       </a>\n       . The biggest challenge with CubeSat propulsion is preventing risk to the launch vehicle and its primary\n       <a href="/wiki/Payload" title="Payload">\n        payload\n       </a>\n       while still providing significant capability.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Components and methods that are commonly used in larger satellites are disallowed or limited and the CubeSat Design Specification (CDS) requires a waiver for pressurization above 1.2 standard\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_(unit)" title="Atmosphere (unit)">\n        atmospheres\n       </a>\n       , over 100 Wh of stored chemical energy, and hazardous materials.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specs_2-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-specs-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Those restrictions pose great challenges for CubeSat propulsion systems, as typical space propulsion systems utilize combinations of high pressures, high energy densities, and hazardous materials. Beyond the restrictions set forth by\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_service_provider" title="Launch service provider">\n        launch service providers\n       </a>\n       , various technical challenges further reduce the usefulness of CubeSat propulsion.\n       <a href="/wiki/Gimbaled_thrust" title="Gimbaled thrust">\n        Gimbaled thrust\n       </a>\n       cannot be used in small engines due to the complexity of gimbaling mechanisms, thrust vectoring must instead be achieved by thrusting asymmetrically in multiple-nozzle propulsion systems or by changing the center of mass relative to the CubeSat\'s geometry with actuated components.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Small motors may also not have room for\n       <a href="/wiki/Throttle" title="Throttle">\n        throttling\n       </a>\n       methods that allow smaller than fully-on thrust, which is important for precision maneuvers such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_rendezvous" title="Space rendezvous">\n        rendezvous\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       CubeSats which require longer life also benefit from propulsion systems, when used for\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_station-keeping" title="Orbital station-keeping">\n        orbit keeping\n       </a>\n       a propulsion system can slow\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_decay" title="Orbital decay">\n        orbital decay\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_gas_thrusters">\n        Cold gas thrusters\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Cold gas thrusters">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold_gas_thruster" title="Cold gas thruster">\n        cold gas thruster\n       </a>\n       typically stores\n       <a href="/wiki/Inert_gas" title="Inert gas">\n        inert gas\n       </a>\n       , such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">\n        nitrogen\n       </a>\n       , in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Pressure_vessel" title="Pressure vessel">\n        pressurized tank\n       </a>\n       and releases the gas through a\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_engine_nozzle" title="Rocket engine nozzle">\n        nozzle\n       </a>\n       to produce thrust. Operation is handled by just a single\n       <a href="/wiki/Valve" title="Valve">\n        valve\n       </a>\n       in most systems, which makes cold gas the simplest useful propulsion technology.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:1-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Cold gas propulsion systems can be very safe since the gases used do not have to be volatile or\n       <a href="/wiki/Corrosive_substance" title="Corrosive substance">\n        corrosive\n       </a>\n       , though some systems opt to feature dangerous gases such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">\n        sulfur dioxide\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This ability to use inert gases is highly advantageous to CubeSats as they are usually restricted from hazardous materials. Unfortunately, only low performance can be achieved with them,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_36-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:1-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       preventing high impulse maneuvers even in low mass CubeSats. Due to this low performance, their use in CubeSats for main propulsion is limited and designers choose higher efficiency systems with only minor increases in complexity. Cold gas systems more often see use in CubeSat attitude control.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Chemical_propulsion">\n        Chemical propulsion\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Chemical propulsion">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_engine" title="Rocket engine">\n        Chemical propulsion\n       </a>\n       systems use a chemical reaction to produce a high-pressure, high-temperature gas that accelerates out of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Propelling_nozzle" title="Propelling nozzle">\n        nozzle\n       </a>\n       . Chemical propellant can be liquid, solid or a hybrid of both. Liquid propellants can be a\n       <a href="/wiki/Monopropellant_rocket" title="Monopropellant rocket">\n        monopropellant\n       </a>\n       passed through a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catalyst" title="Catalyst">\n        catalyst\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a href="/wiki/Liquid-propellant_rocket" title="Liquid-propellant rocket">\n        bipropellant\n       </a>\n       which\n       <a href="/wiki/Combustion" title="Combustion">\n        combusts\n       </a>\n       an\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxidizing_agent" title="Oxidizing agent">\n        oxidizer\n       </a>\n       and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">\n        fuel\n       </a>\n       . The benefits of\n       <a href="/wiki/Monopropellant_rocket" title="Monopropellant rocket">\n        monopropellants\n       </a>\n       are relatively low-complexity/high-thrust output, low power requirements, and high reliability. Monopropellant motors tend to have high thrust while remaining comparatively simple, which also provides high reliability. These motors are practical for CubeSats due to their low power requirements and because their simplicity allows them to be very small. Small\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrazine" title="Hydrazine">\n        hydrazine\n       </a>\n       fueled motors have been developed,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:0-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but may require a waiver to fly due to restrictions on hazardous chemicals set forth in the CubeSat Design Specification.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specs_2-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-specs-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Safer chemical propellants which would not require hazardous chemical waivers are being developed, such as AF-M315 (\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydroxylammonium_nitrate" title="Hydroxylammonium nitrate">\n        hydroxylammonium nitrate\n       </a>\n       ) for which motors are being or have been designed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_38-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:0-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A "Water Electrolysis Thruster" is technically a chemical propulsion system, as it burns\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">\n        hydrogen\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">\n        oxygen\n       </a>\n       which it generates by on-orbit\n       <a href="/wiki/Electrolysis_of_water" title="Electrolysis of water">\n        electrolysis of water\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tethers2015_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Tethers2015-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_propulsion">\n        Electric propulsion\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Electric propulsion">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BIT-3_Iodine_60W_with_BHC-50E.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2489" data-file-width="4865" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BIT-3_Iodine_60W_with_BHC-50E.jpg/220px-BIT-3_Iodine_60W_with_BHC-50E.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BIT-3_Iodine_60W_with_BHC-50E.jpg/330px-BIT-3_Iodine_60W_with_BHC-50E.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BIT-3_Iodine_60W_with_BHC-50E.jpg/440px-BIT-3_Iodine_60W_with_BHC-50E.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BIT-3_Iodine_60W_with_BHC-50E.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Busek\'s BIT-3 ion thruster proposed for NASA\'s Lunar IceCube mission\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       CubeSat\n       <a href="/wiki/Electrically_powered_spacecraft_propulsion" title="Electrically powered spacecraft propulsion">\n        electric propulsion\n       </a>\n       typically uses electric energy to accelerate propellant to high speed, which results in high\n       <a href="/wiki/Specific_impulse" title="Specific impulse">\n        specific impulse\n       </a>\n       . Many of these technologies can be made small enough for use in nanosatellites, and several methods are in development. Types of electric propulsion currently being designed for use in CubeSats include\n       <a href="/wiki/Hall-effect_thruster" title="Hall-effect thruster">\n        Hall-effect thrusters\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ion_thruster" title="Ion thruster">\n        ion thrusters\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Pulsed_plasma_thruster" title="Pulsed plasma thruster">\n        pulsed plasma thrusters\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Colloid_thruster" title="Colloid thruster">\n        electrospray thrusters\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Resistojet_rocket" title="Resistojet rocket">\n        resistojets\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Several notable CubeSat missions plan to use electric propulsion, such as NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_IceCube" title="Lunar IceCube">\n        Lunar IceCube\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LunarIceCube2015_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LunarIceCube2015-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The high efficiency associated with electric propulsion could allow CubeSats to propel themselves to Mars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mars2015_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mars2015-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Electric propulsion systems are disadvantaged in their use of power, which requires the CubeSat to have larger solar cells, more complicated power distribution, and often larger batteries. Furthermore, many electric propulsion methods may still require pressurized tanks to store propellant, which is restricted by the CubeSat Design Specification.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/ESTCube-1" title="ESTCube-1">\n        ESTCube-1\n       </a>\n       used an\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_sail" title="Electric sail">\n        electric solar-wind sail\n       </a>\n       , which is nothing like a solar sail, despite its name. This technology used an\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_field" title="Electric field">\n        electric field\n       </a>\n       to deflect\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protons" title="Protons">\n        protons\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_wind" title="Solar wind">\n        solar wind\n       </a>\n       to produce thrust. It is similar to an\n       <a href="/wiki/Electrodynamic_tether" title="Electrodynamic tether">\n        electrodynamic tether\n       </a>\n       in that the craft only needs to supply electricity to operate.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Solar_sail">\n        Solar sail\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Solar sail">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_sail" title="Solar sail">\n        Solar sails\n       </a>\n       (also called\xc2\xa0light sails\xc2\xa0or\xc2\xa0photon sails) are a form of\xc2\xa0spacecraft propulsion\xc2\xa0using the\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiation_pressure" title="Radiation pressure">\n        radiation pressure\n       </a>\n       (also called solar pressure) from stars to push large ultra-thin mirrors to high speeds, requiring no propellant. Force from a solar sail scales with the sail\'s area, this makes sails well suited for use in CubeSats as their small mass results in the greater acceleration for a given solar sail\'s area. However, solar sails still need to be quite large compared to the satellite, which means useful solar sails must be deployed, adding mechanical complexity and a potential source of failure. This propulsion method is the only one not plagued with restrictions set by the CubeSat Design Specification, as it does not require high pressures, hazardous materials, or significant chemical energy. Few CubeSats have employed a solar sail as its main propulsion and stability in deep space, including the 3U\n       <a href="/wiki/NanoSail-D2" title="NanoSail-D2">\n        NanoSail-D2\n       </a>\n       launched in 2010, and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LightSail-1" title="LightSail-1">\n        LightSail-1\n       </a>\n       in May 2015.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LightSail-2" title="LightSail-2">\n        LightSail-2\n       </a>\n       is scheduled for launch in March 2017,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Name_change_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Name_change-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       while at least two CubeSats that plan to launch on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">\n        Space Launch System\n       </a>\n       \'s first flight in September 2018 are set to use solar sails, the proposed\n       <a href="/wiki/Near-Earth_Asteroid_Scout" title="Near-Earth Asteroid Scout">\n        Near-Earth Asteroid Scout\n       </a>\n       (NEA Scout)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNutt_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-McNutt-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Flashlight" title="Lunar Flashlight">\n        Lunar Flashlight\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Power">\n        Power\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Power">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Winglet_Pumpkin_Solar_Pannels_for_CubeSat.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="678" data-file-width="1024" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Winglet_Pumpkin_Solar_Pannels_for_CubeSat.png/220px-Winglet_Pumpkin_Solar_Pannels_for_CubeSat.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Winglet_Pumpkin_Solar_Pannels_for_CubeSat.png/330px-Winglet_Pumpkin_Solar_Pannels_for_CubeSat.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Winglet_Pumpkin_Solar_Pannels_for_CubeSat.png/440px-Winglet_Pumpkin_Solar_Pannels_for_CubeSat.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Winglet_Pumpkin_Solar_Pannels_for_CubeSat.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Winglet solar panels increase surface area for power generation\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       CubeSats use\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_cell" title="Solar cell">\n        solar cells\n       </a>\n       to convert solar light to electricity that is then stored in rechargeable\n       <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">\n        lithium-ion batteries\n       </a>\n       that provide power during eclipse as well as during peak load times.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These satellites have a limited surface area on their external walls for solar cells assembly, and has to be effectively shared with other parts, such as antennas, optical sensors, camera lens, propulsion systems, and access port. Lithium-ion batteries feature high energy-to-mass ratios, making them well suited to use on mass-restricted spacecraft. Battery charging and discharging is typically handled by a dedicated electrical power system (EPS). Batteries sometimes feature heaters\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       to prevent the battery from reaching dangerously low temperatures which might cause battery and mission failure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Missions with higher power requirements can make use of\n       <a href="/wiki/Attitude_control" title="Attitude control">\n        attitude control\n       </a>\n       to ensure the solar panels remain in their most effective orientation toward the Sun, and further power needs can be met through the addition and orientation of deployed solar arrays. Recent innovations include additional spring-loaded solar arrays that deploy as soon as the satellite is released, as well as arrays that feature\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Thermal_knife&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Thermal knife (page does not exist)">\n        thermal knife\n       </a>\n       mechanisms that would deploy the panels when commanded. CubeSats may not be powered between launch and deployment, and must feature a\n       <a href="/wiki/Remove_before_flight" title="Remove before flight">\n        remove-before-flight\n       </a>\n       pin which cuts all power to prevent operation during loading into the P-POD. Additionally, a deployment switch is actuated while the craft is loaded into a P-POD, cutting power to the spacecraft and is deactivated after exiting the P-POD.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specs_2-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-specs-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">\n        Telecommunications\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Telecommunications">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:190px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Secondary_antennas4.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="307" data-file-width="255" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Secondary_antennas4.gif/188px-Secondary_antennas4.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/be/Secondary_antennas4.gif 1.5x" width="188"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Secondary_antennas4.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Deployable high-gain mesh reflector antenna operating at Ka-band for the Radar in a Cubesat (Raincube).\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The low cost of CubeSats has enabled unprecedented access to space for smaller institutions and organizations but, for most CubeSat forms, the range and available power is limited to about 2W for its communications antennae.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greek_23-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Greek-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grumman2014_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Grumman2014-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They can use radio-communication systems in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Very_high_frequency" title="Very high frequency">\n        VHF\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ultra_high_frequency" title="Ultra high frequency">\n        UHF\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/L_band" title="L band">\n        L-\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/S_band" title="S band">\n        S-\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/C_band_(IEEE)" title="C band (IEEE)">\n        C-\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/X_band" title="X band">\n        X-band\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greek_23-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Greek-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For UHF/VHF transmissions, a single\n       <a href="/wiki/Helical_antenna" title="Helical antenna">\n        helical antenna\n       </a>\n       or four\n       <a href="/wiki/Monopole_antenna" title="Monopole antenna">\n        monopole antennae\n       </a>\n       are deployed by a spring-loaded mechanism.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greek_23-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Greek-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grumman2014_53-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Grumman2014-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Because of tumbling and low power range, radio-communications are a challenge. Many CubeSats use an\n       <a href="/wiki/Omnidirectional_antenna" title="Omnidirectional antenna">\n        omnidirectional\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Monopole_antenna" title="Monopole antenna">\n        monopole\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Dipole_antenna" title="Dipole antenna">\n        dipole antenna\n       </a>\n       built with commercial measuring tape. For more demanding needs, some companies offer\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-gain_antenna" title="High-gain antenna">\n        high-gain antennae\n       </a>\n       for CubeSats, but their deployment and pointing systems are significantly more complex.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greek_23-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Greek-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grumman2014_53-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Grumman2014-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For example,\n       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">\n        MIT\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">\n        JPL\n       </a>\n       are developing an inflatable dish antenna with a useful range to the Moon but appears to be poorly efficient.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InflatableDish_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-InflatableDish-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       JPL has successfully developed\n       <a href="/wiki/X_band" title="X band">\n        X-band\n       </a>\n       and Ka-band high-gain antennas for\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Cube_One" title="Mars Cube One">\n        MarCO\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:3-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:4-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and Radar in a CubeSat (RainCube) missions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_56-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:4-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Antennas">\n        Antennas\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Antennas">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Traditionally,\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        Low Earth Orbit\n       </a>\n       Cubesats use antennas for communication purpose at UHF and S-band. To venture farther in the solar system, larger antennas compatible with the\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA_Deep_Space_Network" title="NASA Deep Space Network">\n        Deep Space Network\n       </a>\n       (X-band and Ka-band) are required.\n       <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">\n        JPL\n       </a>\n       \'s engineers developed several deployable high-gain antennas compatible with 6U-class cubesats for\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Cube_One" title="Mars Cube One">\n        MarCO\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_55-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:3-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:5-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and NEA Scout.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">\n        JPL\n       </a>\n       \'s engineers have also developed a 0.5m mesh reflector antenna operating at Ka-band and compatible with the DSN\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_55-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:3-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_59-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:5-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       that folds in a 1.5U stowage volume. For\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Cube_One" title="Mars Cube One">\n        MarCO\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">\n        JPL\n       </a>\n       \'s antenna engineers designed a Folded Panel Reflectarray (FPR)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       to fit on a 6U Cubesat bus and supports X-band Mars-to-Earth telecommunications at 8kbit/s at 1AU.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Thermal_management">\n        Thermal management\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Thermal management">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Different CubeSat components possess different acceptable temperature ranges, beyond which they may become temporarily or permanently inoperable. Satellites in orbit are heated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermal_radiation" title="Thermal radiation">\n        radiative heat\n       </a>\n       emitted from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">\n        Sun\n       </a>\n       directly and reflected off Earth, as well as heat generated by the craft\'s components. CubeSats must also\n       <a href="/wiki/Radiative_cooling" title="Radiative cooling">\n        cool by radiating heat\n       </a>\n       either into space or into the cooler Earth\'s surface, if it is cooler than the spacecraft. All of these radiative heat sources and sinks are rather constant and very predictable, so long as the CubeSat\'s orbit and eclipse time are known.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Components used to ensure the temperature requirements are met in CubeSats include\n       <a href="/wiki/Multi-layer_insulation" title="Multi-layer insulation">\n        multi-layer insulation\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Heating_element" title="Heating element">\n        heaters\n       </a>\n       for the battery. Other\n       <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft_thermal_control" title="Spacecraft thermal control">\n        spacecraft thermal control\n       </a>\n       techniques in small satellites include specific component placement based on expected thermal output of those components and, rarely, deployed thermal devices such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Louver" title="Louver">\n        louvers\n       </a>\n       . Analysis and simulation of the spacecraft\'s thermal model is an important determining factor in applying thermal management components and techniques. CubeSats with special thermal concerns, often associated with certain deployment mechanisms and payloads, may be tested in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermal_vacuum_chamber" title="Thermal vacuum chamber">\n        thermal vacuum chamber\n       </a>\n       before launch. Such testing provides a larger degree of assurance than full-sized satellites can receive, since CubeSats are small enough to fit inside of a thermal vacuum chamber in their entirety.\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermometer" title="Thermometer">\n        Temperature sensors\n       </a>\n       are typically placed on different CubeSat components so that action may be taken to avoid dangerous temperature ranges, such as reorienting the craft in order to avoid or introduce direct thermal radiation to a specific part, thereby allowing it to cool or heat.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Costs">\n        Costs\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Costs">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       CubeSat forms a cost-effective independent means of getting a payload into orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tiny_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tiny-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After delays from low-cost launchers such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Interorbital_Systems" title="Interorbital Systems">\n        Interorbital Systems\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       launch prices have been about $100,000 per unit,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but newer operators are offering lower pricing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some CubeSats have complicated components or instruments, such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LightSail-1" title="LightSail-1">\n        LightSail-1\n       </a>\n       , that pushes their construction cost into the millions,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but a basic 1U CubeSat can cost about $50,000 to construct\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       so CubeSats are a viable option for some schools and universities; as well as small businesses to develop CubeSats for commercial purposes.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_past_missions">\n        Notable past missions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Notable past missions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_CubeSats" title="List of CubeSats">\n        List of CubeSats\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NanoRacksCubeSatLaunch_ISS038-E-056389.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="146"
