src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/NanoRacksCubeSatLaunch_ISS038-E-056389.jpg/220px-NanoRacksCubeSatLaunch_ISS038-E-056389.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/NanoRacksCubeSatLaunch_ISS038-E-056389.jpg/330px-NanoRacksCubeSatLaunch_ISS038-E-056389.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/NanoRacksCubeSatLaunch_ISS038-E-056389.jpg/440px-NanoRacksCubeSatLaunch_ISS038-E-056389.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NanoRacksCubeSatLaunch_ISS038-E-056389.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/NanoRacks" title="NanoRacks">\n          NanoRacks\n         </a>\n         CubeSats being launched from the\n         <a href="/wiki/NanoRacks_CubeSat_Deployer" title="NanoRacks CubeSat Deployer">\n          NanoRacks CubeSat Deployer\n         </a>\n         on the ISS on February 25, 2014.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       One of the earliest CubeSat launches was on 30 June 2003 from Plesetsk, Russia, with\n       <a href="/wiki/Eurockot_Launch_Services" title="Eurockot Launch Services">\n        Eurockot Launch Services\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <i>\n        Multiple Orbit Mission\n       </i>\n       . CubeSats were put into a\n       <a href="/wiki/Sun-synchronous_orbit" title="Sun-synchronous orbit">\n        Sun-synchronous orbit\n       </a>\n       and included the Danish\n       <a href="/wiki/AAU_CubeSat" title="AAU CubeSat">\n        AAU CubeSat\n       </a>\n       and DTUSat, the Japanese XI-IV and CUTE-1, the Canadian Can X-1, and the US\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quakesat" title="Quakesat">\n        Quakesat\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On February 13, 2012, three PPODs deployers containing seven CubeSats were placed into orbit along with the\n       <a href="/wiki/LARES_(satellite)" title="LARES (satellite)">\n        Lares\n       </a>\n       satellite aboard a\n       <a href="/wiki/Vega_(rocket)" title="Vega (rocket)">\n        Vega\n       </a>\n       rocket launched from French Guiana. The CubeSats launched were\n       <a href="/wiki/E-st@r" title="E-st@r">\n        e-st@r\n       </a>\n       Space (Politecnico di Torino, Italy), Goliat (University of Bucarest, Romania),\n       <a href="/wiki/MaSat-1" title="MaSat-1">\n        MaSat-1\n       </a>\n       (Budapest University of Technology and Economics, Hungary),\n       <a href="/wiki/PW-Sat" title="PW-Sat">\n        PW-Sat\n       </a>\n       (Warsaw University of Technology, Poland), Robusta (University of Montpellier 2, France),\n       <a href="/wiki/UniCubeSat-GG" title="UniCubeSat-GG">\n        UniCubeSat-GG\n       </a>\n       (University of Rome La Sapienza, Italy), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Xatcobeo" title="Xatcobeo">\n        XaTcobeo\n       </a>\n       (University of Vigo and INTA, Spain). The CubeSats were launched in the framework of the "Vega Maiden Flight" opportunity of the European Space Agency.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On September 13, 2012, eleven CubeSats were launched from eight P-PODs, as part of the "OutSat" secondary payload aboard a\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Launch_Alliance" title="United Launch Alliance">\n        United Launch Alliance\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlas_V" title="Atlas V">\n        Atlas V\n       </a>\n       rocket.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This was the largest number of CubeSats (and largest volume of 24U) successfully placed to orbit on a single launch, this was made possible by use of the new NPS CubeSat Launcher system (\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=NPSCuL&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="NPSCuL (page does not exist)">\n        NPSCuL\n       </a>\n       ) developed at the Naval Postgraduate School (NPS). The following CubeSats were placed in orbit: SMDC-ONE 2.2 (Baker), SMDC-ONE 2.1 (Able), AeroCube 4.0(x3), Aeneas,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CSSWE" title="CSSWE">\n        CSSWE\n       </a>\n       , CP5, CXBN, CINEMA, and Re (STARE).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Five CubeSats (\n       <a href="/wiki/Raiko" title="Raiko">\n        Raiko\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Niwaka" title="Niwaka">\n        Niwaka\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/We-Wish" title="We-Wish">\n        We-Wish\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/TechEdSat" title="TechEdSat">\n        TechEdSat\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/F-1_(satellite)" title="F-1 (satellite)">\n        F-1\n       </a>\n       ) were placed into orbit from the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       on October 4, 2012, as a technology demonstration of small satellite deployment from the ISS. They were launched and delivered to ISS as a cargo of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kounotori_3" title="Kounotori 3">\n        Kounotori 3\n       </a>\n       , and an ISS astronaut prepared the deployment mechanism attached to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module" title="Japanese Experiment Module">\n        Japanese Experiment Module\n       </a>\n       \'s robotic arm.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Four CubeSats were deployed from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cygnus_Mass_Simulator" title="Cygnus Mass Simulator">\n        Cygnus Mass Simulator\n       </a>\n       , which was launched April 21, 2013 on the maiden flight of Orbital Sciences\'\n       <a href="/wiki/Antares_(rocket)" title="Antares (rocket)">\n        Antares rocket\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OSSlideBriefing_76-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OSSlideBriefing-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Three of them are 1U\n       <a href="/wiki/PhoneSat" title="PhoneSat">\n        PhoneSats\n       </a>\n       built by NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Ames_Research_Center" title="Ames Research Center">\n        Ames Research Center\n       </a>\n       to demonstrate the use of\n       <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">\n        smart phones\n       </a>\n       as\n       <a href="/wiki/Avionics" title="Avionics">\n        avionics\n       </a>\n       in CubeSats. The fourth was a 3U satellite, called Dove-1, built by\n       <a href="/wiki/Planet_Labs" title="Planet Labs">\n        Planet Labs\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sail-design-types1.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="114" data-file-width="175" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b3/Sail-design-types1.png" width="175"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sail-design-types1.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Diagram showing\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LightSail-1" title="LightSail-1">\n          LightSail\'s\n         </a>\n         orbital configuration\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A total of thirty-three CubeSats were deployed from the ISS on February 11, 2014. Of those thirty-three, twenty-eight were part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Flock-1" title="Flock-1">\n        Flock-1\n       </a>\n       constellation of Earth-imaging CubeSats. Of the other five, two are from other US-based companies, two from Lithuania, and one from Peru.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LightSail-1" title="LightSail-1">\n        LightSail-1\n       </a>\n       is a 3U CubeSat prototype propelled by a\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_sail" title="Solar sail">\n        solar sail\n       </a>\n       . It was launched on 20 May 2015 from Florida. Its four sails are made of very thin\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mylar" title="Mylar">\n        Mylar\n       </a>\n       and have a total area of 32 m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       . This test will allow a full checkout of the satellite\'s systems in advance of the main 2016 mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-planetary20150126_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-planetary20150126-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On October 5, 2015, AAUSAT5 (Aalborg University, Denmark), was deployed from the ISS. launched in the framework of the "Fly Your Satellite!" programme of the European Space Agency.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Miniature_X-ray_Solar_Spectrometer_CubeSat" title="Miniature X-ray Solar Spectrometer CubeSat">\n        Miniature X-ray Solar Spectrometer CubeSat\n       </a>\n       is a 3U launched to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       on 6 December 2015 from where it was deployed on 16 May 2016. It is the first mission launched in the\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       Science Mission Directorate CubeSat Integration Panel,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n        <a href="#cite_note-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which is focused on doing science with CubeSats. As of 12 July 2016, the minimum mission success criteria (one month of science observations) has been met, but the spacecraft continues to perform nominally and observations continue.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Three CubeSats were launched on April 25, 2016 together with Sentinel-1B on a Soyuz rocket VS14 launched from Kourou, French Guiana. The satellites were: AAUSAT4 (Aalborg University, Denmark), e-st@r-II (Politecnico di Torino, Italy) and OUFTI-1 (Universit\xc3\xa9 de Li\xc3\xa8ge, Belgium). The CubeSats were launched in the framework of the "Fly Your Satellite!" programme of the European Space Agency.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On February 15, 2017 Indian Space Research Organisation (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISRO" title="ISRO">\n        ISRO\n       </a>\n       ) set record with the launch of 104 satellites on a single rocket. The launch of\n       <a href="/wiki/PSLV-C37" title="PSLV-C37">\n        PSLV-C37\n       </a>\n       in a single payload, including the Cartosat-2 series and 103 co-passenger satellites, together weighed over 650\xc2\xa0kg (1,433\xc2\xa0lb). Of the 104 satellites, all but three were cubesats. Of the 101 nano satellites, 96 were from the United States and one each from Israel, Kazakhstan, the Netherlands, Switzerland and the United Arab Emirates.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Future_projects">\n        Future projects\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Future projects">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="QB50">\n        QB50\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: QB50">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       QB50 is a proposed international network of 50 CubeSats for multi-point,\n       <i>\n        in-situ\n       </i>\n       measurements in the lower\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermosphere" title="Thermosphere">\n        thermosphere\n       </a>\n       (90\xe2\x80\x93350\xc2\xa0km) and re-entry research. QB50 is an initiative of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Von_Karman_Institute" title="Von Karman Institute">\n        Von Karman Institute\n       </a>\n       and is funded by the European Commission as part of the 7th Framework Programme (FP7). Double-unit (2U) CubeSats (10\xc3\x9710\xc3\x9720\xc2\xa0cm) are developed, with one unit (the \'functional\' unit) providing the usual satellite functions and the other unit (the \'science\' unit) accommodating a set of standardised sensors for lower thermosphere and re-entry research. 35 CubeSats are envisaged to be provided by universities from 22 countries around the world, among them 4 are from the US, 4 from China, 4 from France, 3 from Australia and 3 South Korea.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ten 2U or 3U CubeSats are foreseen to serve for in-orbit technology demonstration of new space technologies.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Request for Proposals (RFP) for the QB50 CubeSat was released on February 15, 2012. Two "precursor" QB50 satellites were launched aboard a\n       <a href="/wiki/Dnepr_(rocket)" title="Dnepr (rocket)">\n        Dnepr rocket\n       </a>\n       on June 19, 2014.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       All 50 CubeSats were supposed to be launched together on a single\n       <a href="/wiki/Tsyklon-4" title="Tsyklon-4">\n        Cyclone-4\n       </a>\n       launch vehicle in February 2016,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but due to the unavailability of the launch vehicle, 40 satellites are now planned to be launched aboard\n       <a href="/wiki/Cygnus_CRS_OA-7" title="Cygnus CRS OA-7">\n        Cygnus CRS OA-7\n       </a>\n       in April 2017 and subsequently deployed from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISS" title="ISS">\n        ISS\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A dozen other cubesats have been manifested on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PSLV-XL" title="PSLV-XL">\n        PSLV-XL\n       </a>\n       C38 mission in May 2017.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="2018_InSight_mission:_MarCO_CubeSats">\n        2018 InSight mission: MarCO CubeSats\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 2018 InSight mission: MarCO CubeSats">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PIA19388-Mars-InSight-MarCO-CubeSats-20150612.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2550" data-file-width="3600" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/PIA19388-Mars-InSight-MarCO-CubeSats-20150612.jpg/220px-PIA19388-Mars-InSight-MarCO-CubeSats-20150612.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/PIA19388-Mars-InSight-MarCO-CubeSats-20150612.jpg/330px-PIA19388-Mars-InSight-MarCO-CubeSats-20150612.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/PIA19388-Mars-InSight-MarCO-CubeSats-20150612.jpg/440px-PIA19388-Mars-InSight-MarCO-CubeSats-20150612.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PIA19388-Mars-InSight-MarCO-CubeSats-20150612.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         An artist\'s rendering of\n         <a href="/wiki/Mars_Cube_One" title="Mars Cube One">\n          MarCO\n         </a>\n         A and B during the descent of\n         <a href="/wiki/InSight" title="InSight">\n          InSight\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The May 2018 launch,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_90-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:2-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/InSight" title="InSight">\n        InSight\n       </a>\n       stationary lander to Mars, will include two CubeSats to flyby Mars to provide additional relay communications from InSight to Earth during entry and landing. This will be the first flight of CubeSats in deep space. The mission CubeSat technology is called\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Cube_One" title="Mars Cube One">\n        Mars Cube One\n       </a>\n       (MarCO), a six-unit CubeSat, 14.4 inches (36.6 centimeters) by 9.5 inches (24.3 centimeters) by 4.6 inches (11.8 centimeters). MarCo is an experiment, but not necessary for the InSight mission, to add relay communications to space missions in important time durations, in this case from the time of InSight atmospheric entry to its landing.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       MarCO will launch in May 2018 with the InSight lander and will separate after launch and then travel in their own trajectories to Mars. After separation, MarCO will deploy two radio antennas and two solar panels. The high-gain,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X-band" title="X-band">\n        X-band\n       </a>\n       antenna is a flat panel to direct radio waves. MarCO will navigate to Mars independently from the InSight lander, making their own course adjustments on the flight.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During InSight\'s planned entry, descent and landing (EDL) in November 2018,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_90-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:2-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the lander will transmit information in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UHF" title="UHF">\n        UHF\n       </a>\n       radio band to NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter">\n        Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter\n       </a>\n       (MRO) flying overhead. MRO will forward EDL information to Earth using a radio frequency in the\n       <a href="/wiki/X_band" title="X band">\n        X band\n       </a>\n       , but cannot simultaneously receive information in one band if transmitting on another. Confirmation of a successful landing could be received on Earth several hours after, so MarCO would be a technology demonstration of real-time telemetry during the landing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="CubeSat_Launch_Initiative">\n        CubeSat Launch Initiative\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: CubeSat Launch Initiative">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       NASA\'s\n       <a class="external text" href="http://www.nasa.gov/directorates/heo/home/CubeSats_initiative" rel="nofollow">\n        CubeSat Launch Initiative\n       </a>\n       , created in 2010 provides CubeSat launch opportunities to educational institutions, non-profit organizations and NASA Centers. Since its inception the CubeSat Launch Initiative has launched 46 CubeSats flown on 12 ELaNa Missions from 28 unique organizations and has selected 119 CubeSat missions from 66 unique organizations.\n       <a class="external text" href="https://www.nasa.gov/mission_pages/smallsats/elana/index.html" rel="nofollow">\n        Educational Launch of Nanosatellites (ELaNa)\n       </a>\n       missions have included: BisonSat the first CubeSat built by a tribal college, TJ3Sat the first CubeSat built by a high school and STMSat-1 the first CubeSat built by an elementary school. NASA releases an\n       <a class="external text" href="http://www.nasa.gov/content/announcement-of-opportunity-for-cubesat-launch-initiative" rel="nofollow">\n        Announcement of Opportunity\n       </a>\n       in August of each year with selections made the following February.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="NASA\'s_Cube_Quest_Challenge">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA.27s_Cube_Quest_Challenge">\n        NASA\'s Cube Quest Challenge\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: NASA\'s Cube Quest Challenge">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       NASA initiated its Cube Quest Challenge in 2015, a competition to foster innovation in the use of CubeSats beyond low Earth orbit. The Cube Quest Challenge, sponsored by NASA\xe2\x80\x99s Space Technology Mission Directorate Centennial Challenge Program, offers a total of $5 million to teams that meet the challenge objectives of designing, building and delivering flight-qualified, small satellites capable of advanced operations near and beyond the Moon. Teams compete for a variety of prizes in lunar orbit or deep space.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Up to three teams competing may be selected to launch their CubeSat design aboard the\n       <a href="/wiki/Exploration_Mission_1" title="Exploration Mission 1">\n        SLS-EM1 mission\n       </a>\n       in 2018.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Fly_Your_Satellite!">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fly_Your_Satellite.21">\n        Fly Your Satellite!\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Fly Your Satellite!">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The recurring CubeSats programme of the Education Office of the European Space Agency where university students have the opportunity to develop and implement their CubeSat mission with support of ESA specialists. Participating student teams can experience the full life cycle of a spacecraft from designing, building, and testing to eventually, the possibility of launching and operating their CubeSat.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_and_deployment">\n        Launch and deployment\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Launch and deployment">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="785" data-file-width="590" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg/220px-Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg/330px-Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg/440px-Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dnepr_rocket_lift-off_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A\n         <a href="/wiki/Dnepr_(rocket)" title="Dnepr (rocket)">\n          Dnepr\n         </a>\n         rocket launching from\n         <a href="/wiki/ISC_Kosmotras" title="ISC Kosmotras">\n          ISC Kosmotras\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Unlike full-sized spacecraft, CubeSats have the ability to be delivered into space as cargo and then deployed by the International Space Station. This presents an alternative method of achieving orbit apart from launch and deployment by a\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_vehicle" title="Launch vehicle">\n        launch vehicle\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/NanoRacks" title="NanoRacks">\n        NanoRacks\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Made_In_Space,_Inc." title="Made In Space, Inc.">\n        Made in Space\n       </a>\n       are developing means of constructing CubeSats on the International Space Station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Current_launch_systems">\n        Current launch systems\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Current launch systems">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       NASA\'s CubeSat Launch Initiative has launched more than 46 CubeSats on its ELaNa missions over the last several years, and as of 2016, 57 are manifested for flight over the next few years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       No matter how inexpensive or versatile CubeSats may be, they must hitch rides as secondary payload on large rockets launching much larger spacecraft, at prices starting around $100,000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dean2015_100-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dean2015-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since CubeSats are deployed by P-PODs and similar deployment systems, they can be integrated and launched into virtually any launch vehicle. However, some launch service providers refuse to launch CubeSats, whether on all launches or only on specific launches, two examples are\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Launch_Services" title="International Launch Services">\n        ILS\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sea_Launch" title="Sea Launch">\n        Sea Launch\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">\n        <a href="#cite_note-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Japan_Manned_Space_Systems_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Japan Manned Space Systems Corporation (page does not exist)">\n        Japan Manned Space Systems Corporation\n       </a>\n       (JAMSS)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n        <a href="#cite_note-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       are two recent companies that offer commercial launch services for CubeSats as secondary payload, but a launch backlog still exists. Additionally, India\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISRO" title="ISRO">\n        ISRO\n       </a>\n       has been commercially launching foreign CubeSats since 2009 as secondary payloads. On 15 Feb 2017, ISRO set the world record by launching 103 CubeSats on board its Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle for various foreign companies\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n        <a href="#cite_note-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/ISC_Kosmotras" title="ISC Kosmotras">\n        ISC Kosmotras\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Eurockot_Launch_Services" title="Eurockot Launch Services">\n        Eurockot\n       </a>\n       also offer launch services for CubeSats.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">\n        <a href="#cite_note-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Future_and_proposed_launch_systems">\n        Future and proposed launch systems\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Future and proposed launch systems">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       On 5 May 2015,\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       announced a program based at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       dedicated to develop a new class of rockets designed specifically to launch very small satellites: the NASA\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Venture_Class_Launch_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Venture Class Launch Services (page does not exist)">\n        Venture Class Launch Services\n       </a>\n       (VCLS),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dean2015_100-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dean2015-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solicitation2015_108-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-solicitation2015-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n        <a href="#cite_note-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which will offer a payload mass of 30\xc2\xa0kg to 60\xc2\xa0kg for each launcher.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solicitation2015_108-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-solicitation2015-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">\n        <a href="#cite_note-110">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Five months later, in October 2015, NASA awarded a total of $17.1 million to three separate startup launch companies for one flight each: $6.9 million to\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_Lab" title="Rocket Lab">\n        Rocket Lab\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_Lab#Electron_launch_vehicle" title="Rocket Lab">\n        Electron rocket\n       </a>\n       ); $5.5 million to\n       <a href="/wiki/Firefly_Space_Systems" title="Firefly Space Systems">\n        Firefly Space Systems\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Firefly_Space_Systems#Firefly_Alpha" title="Firefly Space Systems">\n        Alpha rocket\n       </a>\n       ); and $4.7 million to\n       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Galactic" title="Virgin Galactic">\n        Virgin Galactic\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Galactic#LauncherOne" title="Virgin Galactic">\n        LauncherOne rocket\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Venture2015_111-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Venture2015-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The payloads for the three flights under the VCLS contract have not yet been assigned.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Venture2015_111-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Venture2015-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other small satellite launch systems are under development that would carry CubeSats alongside a small payload, including the\n       <i>\n        Neptune\n       </i>\n       series of rockets by\n       <a href="/wiki/Interorbital_Systems" title="Interorbital Systems">\n        Interorbital Systems\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garvey_Spacecraft" title="Garvey Spacecraft">\n        Garvey Spacecraft\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <i>\n        Nanosat Launch Vehicle\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n        <a href="#cite_note-112">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/SPARK_(rocket)" title="SPARK (rocket)">\n        SPARK\n       </a>\n       rocket. In addition to conventional launch vehicles and launch facilitators like KSF Space, several\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_launch_to_orbit" title="Air launch to orbit">\n        air launch to orbit\n       </a>\n       vehicles are in the works by\n       <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Space_Systems" title="Swiss Space Systems">\n        Swiss Space Systems\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Generation_Orbit_Launch_Services" title="Generation Orbit Launch Services">\n        Generation Orbit Launch Services\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">\n        Boeing\n       </a>\n       (in the form of their\n       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Small_Launch_Vehicle" title="Boeing Small Launch Vehicle">\n        Small Launch Vehicle\n       </a>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of December 2015, only one launch vehicle that emphasizes small CubeSat payloads has made a launch attempt, the\n       <a href="/wiki/SPARK_(rocket)" title="SPARK (rocket)">\n        SPARK\n       </a>\n       , broke up shortly after launch on 4 November 2015. The rocket was carrying 12 CubeSats of various sizes along with its 55 kilogram primary payload.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">\n        <a href="#cite_note-113">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocket_Lab" title="Rocket Lab">\n        Rocket Lab\n       </a>\n       \'s CubeSats are planned to be launched from New Zealand.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n        <a href="#cite_note-114">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Deployment">\n        Deployment\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=CubeSat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Deployment">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CSSWE_CubeSat_and_PPOD_prior_to_integration.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="742" data-file-width="861" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/CSSWE_CubeSat_and_PPOD_prior_to_integration.png/220px-CSSWE_CubeSat_and_PPOD_prior_to_integration.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/CSSWE_CubeSat_and_PPOD_prior_to_integration.png/330px-CSSWE_CubeSat_and_PPOD_prior_to_integration.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/CSSWE_CubeSat_and_PPOD_prior_to_integration.png/440px-CSSWE_CubeSat_and_PPOD_prior_to_integration.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CSSWE_CubeSat_and_PPOD_prior_to_integration.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CSSWE" title="CSSWE">\n          CSSWE\n         </a>\n         next to its P-POD before integration and launch\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       P-PODs were designed with CubeSats to provide a common platform for\n       <a href="/wiki/Secondary_payload" title="Secondary payload">\n        secondary payloads\n       </a>\n       . P-PODs are mounted to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_vehicle" title="Launch vehicle">\n        launch vehicle\n       </a>\n       and carry CubeSats into orbit and deploy them once the proper signal is received from the launch vehicle. The P-POD Mk III has capacity for three 1U CubeSats, or other 0.5U, 1U, 1.5U, 2U, or 3U CubeSats combination up to a maximum volume of 3U.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">\n        <a href="#cite_note-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other CubeSat deployers exist, with the NanoRacks CubeSat Deployer (NRCSD) on the International Space Station being the most popular method of CubeSat deployment as of 2014.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-database_3-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-database-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some CubeSat deployers are created by companies, such as the ISIPOD (Innovative Solutions In Space BV) or SPL (Astro und Feinwerktechnik Adlershof GmbH), while some have been created by governments or other non-profit institutions such as the X-POD (\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">\n        University of Toronto\n       </a>\n       ), T-POD (\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tokyo" title="University of Tokyo">\n        University of Tokyo\n       </a>\n       ), or the J-SSOD (\n       <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">\n        JAXA\n       </a>\n       ) on the International Space Station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While the P-POD is limited to launching a 3U CubeSat at most, the NRCSD can launch a 6U (10\xc3\x9710\xc3\x9768.1\xc2\xa0cm) CubeSat and the ISIPOD can launch a different form of 6U CubeSat (10\xc3\x9722.63\xc3\x9734.05\xc2\xa0cm).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While nearly all CubeSats are deployed from a launch vehicle or the International Space Station, some are deployed by the primary payloads themselves. For example,\n       <a href="/wiki/FASTSAT" title="FASTSAT">\n        FASTSAT\n       </a>\n       deployed the\n       <a href="/wiki/NanoSail-D2" title="NanoSail-D2">\n        NanoSail-D2\n       </a>\n       , a 3U CubeSat. This was done again with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cygnus_Mass_Simulator" title="Cygnus Mass Simulator">\n        Cygnus Mass Simulator\n       </a>\n       as the primary payload launched on the maiden flight of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Antares_(rocket)" title="Antares (rocket)">\n        Antares\n       </a>\n       rocket, carrying and later deploying four CubeSats. For CubeSat applications beyond Earth\'s orbit, the method of deploying the satellites from the primary payload will also be adopted. Eleven CubeSats are planned to be launched on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">\n        Space Launch System\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Exploration_Mission_1" title="Exploration Mission 1">\n        Exploration Mission 1\n       </a>\n       , which would place them in the vicinity of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">\n        Moon\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Insight" title="Insight">\n        Insight\n       </a>\n       , a planned\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">\n        Mars\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Lander_(spacecraft)" title="Lander (spacecraft)">\n        lander\n       </a>\n       , will also bring CubeSats beyond Earth orbit to use them as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communications_satellites" title="Communications satellites">\n        relay communications satellites\n       </a>\n       . Known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Cube_One" title="Mars Cube One">\n        MarCO\n       </a>\n       A and B, they would be the first CubeSats sent beyond the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%E2%80%93Moon_system" title="Earth\xe2\x80\x93Moon system">\n        Earth\xe2\x80\x93Moon system\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Chasqui_I" title="Chasqui I">\n        Chasqui I\n       </a>\n       saw a unique deployment process, when it was deployed by hand during a spacewalk on the International Space Station in 2014.\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span            <a href="/wiki/Jordi_Puig-Suari" title="Jordi Puig-Suari">\n              Jordi Puig-Suari\n             </a>\n             of\n             <a href="/wiki/California_Polytechnic_State_University" title="California Polytechnic State University">\n              California Polytechnic State University\n             </a>\n             and\n          Stanford University\n             </a>\n             invented the CubeSat, they never imagined that the tiny satellites would be adopted by universities, companies and government agencies around the world. They simply wanted to design a spacecraft with capabilities similar to\n             <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sputnik" title="Sputnik">\n              Sputnik\n             </a>\n             that graduate student could design, build, test and operate.
